{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01HVwNDLuzdmdZcjY56h9Vgv","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: package fairqueuing\\n18: \\n19: import (\\n20: \\t\\\"context\\\"\\n21: \\n22: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/debug\\\"\\n23: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics\\\"\\n24: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request\\\"\\n25: )\\n26: \\n27: // QueueSetFactory is used to create QueueSet objects.  Creation, like\\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\\n33: \\t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\\n34: \\t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\\n35: \\t// execution covering just the regular phase.\\n36: \\t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\\n37: \\t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\\n38: \\t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\\n39: \\t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\\n40: \\t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\\n41: \\tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n42: }\\n43: \\n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\\n47: \\t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\\n48: \\t// dispatching configuration.\\n49: \\tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\\n54: // functionality described in the \\\"Assignment to a Queue\\\", \\\"Queuing\\\",\\n55: // and \\\"Dispatching\\\" sections of\\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\\n58: // today is not that day.\\n59: type QueueSet interface {\\n60: \\t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\\n61: \\t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\\n62: \\t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\\n63: \\t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\\n64: \\t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\\n65: \\t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\\n66: \\t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\\n67: \\t// and until it is undesired and empty.\\n68: \\tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n69: \\n70: \\t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\\n71: \\t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\\n72: \\t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\\n73: \\t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\\n74: \\t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\\n75: \\t// from false to true.\\n76: \\tIsIdle() bool\\n77: \\n78: \\t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\\n79: \\t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\\n80: \\t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\\n81: \\t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\\n82: \\t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\\n83: \\t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\\n84: \\t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\\n85: \\t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\\n86: \\t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\\n87: \\t// was idle at the moment of the return. \\n27: // QueueSetFactory is used to create QueueSet objects.  Creation, like\\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\\n33: \\t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\\n34: \\t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\\n35: \\t// execution covering just the regular phase.\\n36: \\t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\\n37: \\t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\\n38: \\t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\\n39: \\t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\\n40: \\t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\\n41: \\tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n42: }\\n43: \\n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\\n47: \\t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\\n48: \\t// dispatching configuration.\\n49: \\tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level. The fields listed before the lock\n71: // should not be changed; the fields listed after the\n72: // lock must be accessed only while holding the lock.\n73: //\n74: // The methods of this type follow the naming convention that the\n75: // suffix \"Locked\" means the caller must hold the lock; for a method\n76: // whose name does not end in \"Locked\" either acquires the lock or\n77: // does not care about locking.\n78: //\n79: // The methods of this type also follow the convention that the suffix\n80: // \"ToBoundLocked\" means that the caller may have to follow up with a\n81: // call to `boundNextDispatchLocked`. At this first level of development this controller\\n70: // takes the simplest possible approach: whenever notified of any\\n71: // change to any config object, or when any priority level that is\\n72: // undesired becomes completely unused, all the config objects are\\n73: // read and processed as a whole.\\n74: \\n75: const (\\n76: \\t// Borrowing among priority levels will be accomplished by periodically\\n77: \\t// adjusting the current concurrency limits (CurrentCLs);\\n78: \\t// borrowingAdjustmentPeriod is that period.\\n79: \\tborrowingAdjustmentPeriod = 10 * time.Second\\n80: \\n81: \\t// The input to the seat borrowing is smoothed seat demand figures.\\n82: \\t// This constant controls the decay rate of that smoothing,\\n83: \\t// as described in the comment on the `seatDemandStats` field of `priorityLevelState`.\\n84: \\t// The particular number appearing here has the property that half-life\\n85: \\t// of that decay is 5 minutes.\\n86: \\t// This is a very preliminary guess at a good value and is likely to be tweaked\\n87: \\t// once we get some experience with borrowing.\\n88: \\tseatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977\\n89: )\\n90: \\n91: // The funcs in this package follow the naming convention that the suffix\\n92: // \\\"Locked\\\" means the relevant mutex must be locked at the start of each\\n93: // call and will be locked upon return.  For a configController, the\\n94: // suffix \\\"ReadLocked\\\" stipulates a read lock while just \\\"Locked\\\"\\n95: // stipulates a full lock.  Absence of either suffix means that either\\n96: // (a) the lock must NOT be held at call time and will not be held\\n97: // upon return or (b) locking is irrelevant.\\n98: \\n99: // StartFunction begins the process of handling a request.  If the\\n100: // request gets queued then this function uses the given hashValue as\\n101: // the source of entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a\\n102: // queue.  The descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but\\n103: // appear in log messages.  This method does not return until the\\n104: // queuing, if any, for this request is done. This controller does not enforce\\n158: \\t// any limits on max seats stored in this tracker, it is up to the work estimator\\n159: \\t// to set lower/upper limits on max seats (currently min=1, max=10).\\n160: \\tMaxSeatsTracker\\n161: \\n162: \\t// the most recent update attempts, ordered by increasing age.\\n163: \\t// Consumer trims to keep only the last minute's worth of entries.\\n164: \\t// The controller uses this to limit itself to at most six updates\\n165: \\t// to a given FlowSchema in any minute.\\n166: \\t// This may only be accessed from the one and only worker goroutine.\\n167: \\tmostRecentUpdates []updateAttempt\\n168: \\n169: \\t// This must be locked while accessing the later fields.\\n170: \\t// A lock for writing is needed\\n171: \\t// for writing to any of the following:\\n172: \\t// - the flowSchemas field\\n173: \\t// - the slice held in the flowSchemas field\\n174: \\t// - the priorityLevelStates field\\n175: \\t// - the map held in the priorityLevelStates field\\n176: \\t// - any field of a priorityLevelState held in that map\\n177: \\tlock sync.RWMutex\\n178: \\n179: \\t// flowSchemas holds the flow schema objects, sorted by increasing\\n180: \\t// numerical (decreasing logical) matching precedence. \\t// and `queues`.\\n209: \\tqsCompleter fq.QueueSetCompleter\\n210: \\n211: \\t// The QueueSet for this priority level.\\n212: \\t// Never nil.\\n213: \\tqueues fq.QueueSet\\n214: \\n215: \\t// One QueueSet is a set of queues operating\\n19: // according to this technique.\\n20: //\\n21: // Fair queuing for server requests is inspired by the fair queuing\\n22: // technique from the world of networking.  You can find a good paper\\n23: // on that at https://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?doid=75247.75248 or\\n24: // http://people.csail.mit.edu/imcgraw/links/research/pubs/networks/WFQ.pdf\\n25: // and there is an implementation outline in the Wikipedia article at\\n26: // https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_queuing .\\n27: //\\n28: // Fair queuing for server requests differs from traditional fair\\n29: // queuing in three ways: (1) we are dispatching application layer\\n30: // requests to a server rather than transmitting packets on a network\\n31: // link, (2) multiple requests can be executing at once, and (3) the\\n32: // service time (execution duration) is not known until the execution\\n33: // completes.\\n34: //\\n35: // The first two differences can easily be handled by straightforward\\n36: // adaptation of the concept called \\\"R(t)\\\" in the original paper and\\n37: // \\\"virtual time\\\" in the implementation outline. In that\\n38: // implementation outline, the notation now() is used to mean reading\\n39: // the virtual clock. In the original paper’s terms, \\\"R(t)\\\" is the\\n40: // number of \\\"rounds\\\" that have been completed at real time t ---\\n41: // where a round consists of virtually transmitting one bit from every\\n42: // non-empty queue in the router (regardless of which queue holds the\\n43: // packet that is really being transmitted at the moment); in this\\n44: // conception, a packet is considered to be \\\"in\\\" its queue until the\\n45: // packet’s transmission is finished. For our problem, we can define a\\n46: // round to be giving one nanosecond of CPU to every non-empty queue\\n47: // in the apiserver (where emptiness is judged based on both queued\\n48: // and executing requests from that queue), and define R(t) = (server\\n49: // start time) + (1 ns) * (number of rounds since server start). Let\\n50: // us write NEQ(t) for that number of non-empty queues in the\\n51: // apiserver at time t.  Let us also write C for the concurrency\\n52: // limit.  In the original paper, the partial derivative of R(t) with\\n53: // respect to t is\\n54: //\\n55: //\\t1 / NEQ(t) .\\n56: //\\n57: // To generalize from transmitting one packet at a time to executing C\\n58: // requests at a time, that derivative becomes\\n59: //\\n60: //\\tC / NEQ(t) .\\n61: //\\n62: // However, sometimes there are fewer than C requests available to\\n63: // execute.  For a given queue \\\"q\\\", let us also write \\\"reqs(q, t)\\\" for\\n64: // the number of requests of that queue that are executing at that\\n65: // time.  The total number of requests executing is sum[over q]\\n66: // reqs(q, t) and if that is less than C then virtual time is not\\n67: // advancing as fast as it would if all C seats were occupied; in this\\n68: // case the numerator of the quotient in that derivative should be\\n69: // adjusted proportionally.  Putting it all together for fair queing\\n70: // for server requests: at a particular time t, the partial derivative\\n71: // of R(t) with respect to t is\\n72: //\\n73: //\\tmin( C, sum[over q] reqs(q, t) ) / NEQ(t) .\\n74: //\\n75: // In terms of the implementation outline, this is the rate at which\\n76: // virtual time is advancing at time t (in virtual nanoseconds per\\n77: // real nanosecond). Where the networking implementation outline adds\\n78: // packet size to a virtual time, in our version this corresponds to\\n79: // adding a service time (i.e., duration) to virtual time.\\n80: //\\n81: // The third difference is handled by modifying the algorithm to\\n82: // dispatch based on an initial guess at the request’s service time\\n83: // (duration) and then make the corresponding adjustments once the\\n84: // request’s actual service time is known. This is similar, although\\n85: // not exactly isomorphic, to the original paper’s adjustment by\\n86: // `$\\\\delta$` for the sake of promptness.\\n87: //\\n88: // For implementation simplicity (see below), let us use the same\\n89: // initial service time guess for every request; call that duration\\n90: // G. A good choice might be the service time limit (1\\n91: // minute). Different guesses will give slightly different dynamics,\\n92: // but any positive number can be used for G without ruining the\\n93: // long-term behavior.\\n94: //\\n95: // As in ordinary fair queuing, there is a bound on divergence from\\n96: // the ideal. In plain fair queuing the bound is one packet; in our\\n97: // version it is C requests.\\n98: //\\n99: // To support efficiently making the necessary adjustments once a\\n100: // request’s actual service time is known, the virtual finish time of\\n101: // a request and the last virtual finish time of a queue are not\\n102: // represented directly but instead computed from queue length,\\n103: // request position in the queue, and an alternate state variable that\\n104: // holds the queue’s virtual start time. While the queue is empty and\\n105: // has no requests executing: the value of its virtual start time\\n106: // variable is ignored and its last virtual finish time is considered\\n107: // to be in the virtual past. When a request arrives to an empty queue\\n108: // with no requests executing, the queue’s virtual start time is set\\n109: // to the current virtual time. The virtual finish time of request\\n110: // number J in the queue (counting from J=1 for the head) is J * G +\\n111: // (queue's virtual start time). While the queue is non-empty: the\\n112: // last virtual finish time of the queue is the virtual finish time of\\n113: // the last request in the queue. While the queue is empty and has a\\n114: // request executing: the last virtual finish time is the queue’s\\n115: // virtual start time. When a request is dequeued for service the\\n116: // queue’s virtual start time is advanced by G. When a request\\n117: // finishes being served, and the actual service time was S, the\\n118: // queue’s virtual start time is decremented by G - S.\\n119: package queueset\\n120: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/doc.go\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ef71afa5-d1cf-4452-bf6b-bd7777fb1002","uuid":"1de538f0-9ec0-4031-ab14-b395cbf456c6","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: // Package queueset implements a technique called \\\"fair queuing for\\n18: // server requests\\\". One QueueSet is a set of queues operating\n19: // according to this technique.\n20: //\n21: // Fair queuing for server requests is inspired by the fair queuing\n22: // technique from the world of networking.  You can find a good paper\n23: // on that at https://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?doid=75247.75248 or\n24: // http://people.csail.mit.edu/imcgraw/links/research/pubs/networks/WFQ.pdf\n25: // and there is an implementation outline in the Wikipedia article at\n26: // https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_queuing .\n27: //\n28: // Fair queuing for server requests differs from traditional fair\n29: // queuing in three ways: (1) we are dispatching application layer\n30: // requests to a server rather than transmitting packets on a network\n31: // link, (2) multiple requests can be executing at once, and (3) the\n32: // service time (execution duration) is not known until the execution\n33: // completes.\n34: //\n35: // The first two differences can easily be handled by straightforward\n36: // adaptation of the concept called \"R(t)\" in the original paper and\n37: // \"virtual time\" in the implementation outline. In that\n38: // implementation outline, the notation now() is used to mean reading\n39: // the virtual clock. In the original paper’s terms, \"R(t)\" is the\n40: // number of \"rounds\" that have been completed at real time t ---\n41: // where a round consists of virtually transmitting one bit from every\n42: // non-empty queue in the router (regardless of which queue holds the\n43: // packet that is really being transmitted at the moment); in this\n44: // conception, a packet is considered to be \"in\" its queue until the\n45: // packet’s transmission is finished. For our problem, we can define a\n46: // round to be giving one nanosecond of CPU to every non-empty queue\n47: // in the apiserver (where emptiness is judged based on both queued\n48: // and executing requests from that queue), and define R(t) = (server\n49: // start time) + (1 ns) * (number of rounds since server start). Let\n50: // us write NEQ(t) for that number of non-empty queues in the\n51: // apiserver at time t.  Let us also write C for the concurrency\n52: // limit.  In the original paper, the partial derivative of R(t) with\n53: // respect to t is\n54: //\n55: //\t1 / NEQ(t) .\n56: //\n57: // To generalize from transmitting one packet at a time to executing C\n58: // requests at a time, that derivative becomes\n59: //\n60: //\tC / NEQ(t) .\n61: //\n62: // However, sometimes there are fewer than C requests available to\n63: // execute.  For a given queue \"q\", let us also write \"reqs(q, t)\" for\n64: // the number of requests of that queue that are executing at that\n65: // time.  The total number of requests executing is sum[over q]\n66: // reqs(q, t) and if that is less than C then virtual time is not\n67: // advancing as fast as it would if all C seats were occupied; in this\n68: // case the numerator of the quotient in that derivative should be\n69: // adjusted proportionally.  Putting it all together for fair queing\n70: // for server requests: at a particular time t, the partial derivative\n71: // of R(t) with respect to t is\n72: //\n73: //\tmin( C, sum[over q] reqs(q, t) ) / NEQ(t) .\n74: //\n75: // In terms of the implementation outline, this is the rate at which\n76: // virtual time is advancing at time t (in virtual nanoseconds per\n77: // real nanosecond). Where the networking implementation outline adds\n78: // packet size to a virtual time, in our version this corresponds to\n79: // adding a service time (i.e., duration) to virtual time.\n80: //\n81: // The third difference is handled by modifying the algorithm to\n82: // dispatch based on an initial guess at the request’s service time\n83: // (duration) and then make the corresponding adjustments once the\n84: // request’s actual service time is known. This is similar, although\n85: // not exactly isomorphic, to the original paper’s adjustment by\n86: // `$\\delta$` for the sake of promptness.\n87: //\n88: // For implementation simplicity (see below), let us use the same\n89: // initial service time guess for every request; call that duration\n90: // G. A good choice might be the service time limit (1\n91: // minute). Different guesses will give slightly different dynamics,\n92: // but any positive number can be used for G without ruining the\n93: // long-term behavior.\n94: //\n95: // As in ordinary fair queuing, there is a bound on divergence from\n96: // the ideal. In plain fair queuing the bound is one packet; in our\n97: // version it is C requests.\n98: //\n99: // To support efficiently making the necessary adjustments once a\n100: // request’s actual service time is known, the virtual finish time of\n101: // a request and the last virtual finish time of a queue are not\n102: // represented directly but instead computed from queue length,\n103: // request position in the queue, and an alternate state variable that\n104: // holds the queue’s virtual start time. While the queue is empty and\n105: // has no requests executing: the value of its virtual start time\n106: // variable is ignored and its last virtual finish time is considered\n107: // to be in the virtual past. When a request arrives to an empty queue\n108: // with no requests executing, the queue’s virtual start time is set\n109: // to the current virtual time. The virtual finish time of request\n110: // number J in the queue (counting from J=1 for the head) is J * G +\n111: // (queue's virtual start time). While the queue is non-empty: the\n112: // last virtual finish time of the queue is the virtual finish time of\n113: // the last request in the queue. While the queue is empty and has a\n114: // request executing: the last virtual finish time is the queue’s\n115: // virtual start time. When a request is dequeued for service the\n116: // queue’s virtual start time is advanced by G. When a request\n117: // finishes being served, and the actual service time was S, the\n118: // queue’s virtual start time is decremented by G - S.\n119: package queueset\n120: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/doc.go"}}}

allocProblemItem is one of the classes to which computeConcurrencyAllocation should make an allocation\n27: type allocProblemItem struct {\n28: \ttarget     float64\n29: \tlowerBound float64\n30: \tupperBound float64\n31: }\n32: \n33: // relativeAllocItem is like allocProblemItem but with target avoiding zero and the bounds divided by the target\n34: type relativeAllocItem struct {\n35: \ttarget             float64\n36: \trelativeLowerBound float64\n37: \trelativeUpperBound float64\n38: }\n39: \n40: // relativeAllocProblem collects together all the classes and holds the result of sorting by increasing bounds.\n41: // For J <= K, ascendingIndices[J] identifies a bound that is <= the one of ascendingIndices[K].\n42: // When ascendingIndices[J] = 2*N + 0, this identifies the lower bound of items[N].\n43: // When ascendingIndices[J] = 2*N + 1, this identifies the upper bound of items[N].\n44: type relativeAllocProblem struct {\n45: \titems            []relativeAllocItem\n46: \tascendingIndices []int\n47: }\n48: \n49: // initIndices fills in ascendingIndices and sorts them\n50: func (rap *relativeAllocProblem) initIndices() *relativeAllocProblem {\n51: \trap.ascendingIndices = make([]int, len(rap.items)*2)\n52: \tfor idx := 0; idx < len(rap.ascendingIndices); idx++ {\n53: \t\trap.ascendingIndices[idx] = idx\n54: \t}\n55: \tsort.Sort(rap)\n56: \treturn rap\n57: }\n58: \n59: func (rap *relativeAllocProblem) getItemIndex(idx int) (int, bool) {\n60: \tpackedIndex := rap.ascendingIndices[idx]\n61: \titemIndex := packedIndex / 2\n62: \treturn itemIndex, packedIndex == itemIndex*2\n63: }\n64: \n65: // decode(J) returns the bound associated with ascendingIndices[J], the associated items index,\n66: // and a bool indicating whether the bound is the item's lower bound.\n67: func (rap *relativeAllocProblem) decode(idx int) (float64, int, bool) {\n68: \titemIdx, lower := rap.getItemIndex(idx)\n69: \tif lower {\n70: \t\treturn rap.items[itemIdx].relativeLowerBound, itemIdx, lower\n71: \t}\n72: \treturn rap.items[itemIdx].relativeUpperBound, itemIdx, lower\n73: }\n74: \n75: func (rap *relativeAllocProblem) getProportion(idx int) float64 {\n76: \tprop, _, _ := rap.decode(idx)\n77: \treturn prop\n78: }\n79: \n80: func (rap *relativeAllocProblem) Len() int { return len(rap.items) * 2 }\n81: \n82: func (rap *relativeAllocProblem) Less(i, j int) bool {\n83: \treturn rap.getProportion(i) < rap.getProportion(j)\n84: }\n85: \n86: func (rap *relativeAllocProblem) Swap(i, j int) {\n87: \trap.ascendingIndices[i], rap.ascendingIndices[j] = rap.ascendingIndices[j], rap.ascendingIndices[i]\n88: }\n89: \n90: // minMax records the minimum and maximum value seen while scanning a set of numbers\n91: type minMax struct {\n92: \tmin float64\n93: \tmax float64\n94: }\n95: \n96: // note scans one more number\n97: func (mm *minMax) note(x float64) {\n98: \tmm.min = math.Min(mm.min, x)\n99: \tmm.max = math.Max(mm.max, x)\n100: }\n101: \n102: const MinTarget = 0.001\n103: const epsilon = 0.0000001\n104: \n105: // computeConcurrencyAllocation returns the unique `allocs []float64`, and\n106: // an associated `fairProp float64`, that jointly have\n107: // all of the following properties (to the degree that floating point calculations allow)\n108: // if possible otherwise returns an error saying why it is impossible.\n109: // `allocs` sums to `requiredSum`.\n110: // For each J in [0, len(classes)):\n111: //  1. `classes[J].lowerBound <= allocs[J] <= classes[J].upperBound` and\n112: //  2. exactly one of the following is true:\n113: //     2a. `allocs[J] == fairProp * classes[J].target`,\n114: //     2b. `allocs[J] == classes[J].lowerBound && classes[J].lowerBound > have `target >= lowerBound >= 0` and `upperBound >= lowerBound`.\n118: // A target smaller than MinTarget is treated as if it were MinTarget.\n119: func computeConcurrencyAllocation(requiredSum int, classes []allocProblemItem) ([]float64, float64, error) {\n120: \tif requiredSum < 0 {\n121: \t\treturn nil, 0, errors.New(\"negative sums are not supported\")\n122: \t}\n123: \trequiredSumF := `sensitiveTargetSum`.\n208: \tfor sumSoFar < requiredSumF {\n209: \t\t// There might be more than one bound that is equal to the current value\n210: \t\t// of fairProp; find all of them because they I have enough information to write a detailed deep-dive document.\n\nLet me organize what I've learned:\n\n1. **Purpose and Boundaries**:\n   - APF (Advanced Priority and Fairness) controls request rate on the API server\n   - Uses fair queuing for server requests\n   - Fair queuing is adapted from networking (weighted fair queuing)\n   - Sits in the request pipeline before authentication and authorization\n   - Two main components: FlowSchema (request classification) and PriorityLevelConfiguration (resource allocation)\n\n2. **Key Components**:\n   - `configController` (apf_controller.go): Manages the overall APF configuration and sync with API objects\n   - `queueSet` (queueset.go): Implements the actual queuing and dispatching for one priority level\n   - `queueSetFactory` and `queueSetCompleter`: Factory pattern for creating/reconfiguring queues\n   - `request`: Wrapper around HTTP requests with fairqueuing metadata\n   - `queue`: FIFO queue with virtual time tracking\n   - `flowControl.Filter`: HTTP middleware that integrates APF into request pipeline\n   - `Integrator`: Tracks seat demand statistics for borrowing decisions\n   - Work estimator: Estimates the \"width\" (seats) required by a request\n   - `rule.go`: Matches requests to FlowSchemas\n\n3. **Flow**:\n   - Request arrives at filter\n   - Filter classifies request using FlowSchema matching\n   - Request delegated to corresponding QueueSet for the PriorityLevel\n   - QueueSet uses shuffle sharding to pick queue\n   - Request enqueued or executed based on virtual time fairness\n   - Virtual time advances: min(C, sum(reqs)) / NEQ(t)\n   - Dispatch uses round-robin across queues, selecting minimum virtual finish time\n   \n4. **Fairness Tradeoffs**:\n   - Virtual time calculation balances fairness against real-time variations\n   - Concurrency limits are allocated per priority level\n   - Borrowing mechanism uses a smoothing coefficient to prevent oscillation\n   - Initial work estimates may differ from actual service time\n   - Shuffle sharding width (HandSize) determines how randomly requests distribute across queues\n\n5. **Failure modes and limits**:\n   - Queue length limits prevent unbounded memory growth\n   - Concurrency limits per priority level enforce resource boundaries\n   - Epoch advancement when R overflows prevents numeric issues\n   - Requests are rejected when queue is full and concurrency is at limit\n   - Queued requests timeout or cancel if their context expires\n\n6. **Extension points**:\n   - Custom work estimators can be implemented for different request types\n   - Shuffle sharding parameters are configurable\n   - Seat demand integrator handles the borrowing logic\n   - Promise factory enables {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016K1BFguPb5jSVqgeqbUmfG","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01UPaL4sK4UM4nwX6FY9rfJr","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# APF QueueSet Subsystem: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe Advanced Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet subsystem implements weighted fair queuing on the Kubernetes API server to provide request pacing and priority isolation. Each priority level is served by a QueueSet that dispatches requests according to virtual time fairness, ensuring that under congestion, all active queues make progress proportionally to their configured concurrency weights. This document traces the architectural boundaries, data flow, algorithmic mechanics, operational tradeoffs, and extension points of this subsystem.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### 1.1 Purpose\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem enforces request fairness and priority isolation at the API server level by:\n\n1. **Queuing requests** when they arrive faster than the server can serve them\n2. **Dispatching requests fairly** using weighted fair queuing adapted for server requests (where multiple requests can execute concurrently and work duration is unknown until completion)\n3. **Isolating priority levels** so that high-priority flows cannot starve low-priority flows\n4. **Handling work heterogeneity** by estimating per-request \"width\" (seats) to account for different computational costs\n\n### 1.2 Architectural Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- **HTTP Request Pipeline** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go:155-198`): The APF filter intercepts incoming requests, performs flow classification, and invokes the QueueSet\n- **FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration API objects**: These control-plane objects define request routing policies and resource allocations\n- **Work Estimator** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go:72-136`): Estimates request work based on request type (list, watch, mutating operations)\n- **Authentication/Authorization**: Runs after APF in the request pipeline\n\n**Downstream Components:**\n- **QueueSet**: The core queuing and dispatching engine per priority level\n- **Shuffle Sharding** (`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding`): Distributes requests across queue selections\n- **Metrics/Observability** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics/`): Tracks concurrency, queue lengths, wait times\n- **Watch Tracker** and **MaxSeatsTracker**: Support watch request initialization signaling and per-priority-level seat limits\n\n### 1.3 Configuration Management\n\nThe `configController` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go:99-194`) manages two types of configuration objects:\n\n1. **FlowSchemas**: Define matching criteria (subjects, resources, verbs, non-resource URLs) to classify requests into flows\n2. **PriorityLevelConfigurations**: Define resource allocations (concurrency limits, queue parameters) for each priority level\n\nThe controller maintains eventual consistency with these API objects through informer-based event handlers and a work queue for reprocessing on configuration changes.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Partition\n\n### 2.1 Core Component Hierarchy\n\n```\nconfigController (apf_controller.go)\n├── priorityLevelState (one per PriorityLevelConfiguration)\n│   ├── QueueSet (queueset.go - the main engine)\n│   │   ├── queue[] (virtual time queuing structures)\n│   │   │   ├── requestsWaiting (FIFO linked list)\n│   │   │   └── requestsExecuting (set tracking concurrent requests)\n│   │   ├── currentR (global progress meter / virtual time)\n│   │   ├── Integrator (seat demand statistics)\n│   │   └── Dealer (shuffle sharding for queue selection)\n│   ├── seatDemandStats (for borrowing decisions)\n│   └── Metrics (concurrency and seat gauges)\n└── flowSchemas[] (sorted by matching precedence)\n```\n\n### 2.2 Request Lifecycle Components\n\n| Component | Location | Responsibility |\n|-----------|----------|-----------------|\n| **APF Filter** | `apf_filter.go:155-198` | HTTP middleware; invokes Handle() on each incoming request |\n| **Request Digest** | `apf_controller.go:110-114` | Lightweight request metadata (user, request info) for classification |\n| **Rule Matcher** | `rule.go:28-149` | FlowSchema matching logic; extracts user, resource rules, non-resource rules |\n| **Work Estimator** | `request/width.go:72-136` | Estimates InitialSeats and FinalSeats based on request type |\n| **request struct** | `queueset/types.go:31-83` | Tracks request state through queuing and execution (arrival time, virtual time, queue position) |\n| **queue struct** | `queueset/types.go:91-110` | Per-queue state: FIFO waiting, virtual start time, executing requests |\n\n### 2.3 Virtual Time and Fairness Components\n\n| Component | Location | Responsibility |\n|-----------|----------|-----------------|\n| **currentR (progress meter)** | `queueset.go:119` | Global virtual time counter; advances as requests execute |\n| **nextDispatchR (queue virtual start)** | `queueset/types.go:97-99` | Virtual start time for requests in each queue; enables per-queue virtual finish time calculation |\n| **arrivalR (request virtual time)** | `queueset/types.go:74-76` | Virtual time at which request arrived; used for virtual finish calculation |\n| **totalWork (request work estimate)** | `queueset/types.go:86-88` | Total work in seat-seconds: (initialSeats × estimatedServiceDuration) + (finalSeats × additionalLatency) |\n\n### 2.4 Concurrency Allocation Components\n\n| Component | Location | Responsibility |\n|-----------|----------|-----------------|\n| **nominalCL** | `apf_controller.go:242-243` | Configured concurrency limit for a priority level |\n| **currentCL** | `apf_controller.go:251-252` | Dynamically adjusted concurrency limit (with borrowing) |\n| **minCL, maxCL** | `apf_controller.go:245-249` | Lower and upper bounds for borrowing adjustments |\n| **seatDemandIntegrator** | `apf_controller.go:230` | Tracks time-weighted seat demand (avg, std dev, high watermark) |\n| **computeConcurrencyAllocation** | `conc_alloc.go:119-257` | Solves fair allocation problem: distributes server concurrency among priority levels respecting bounds and fairness |\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Configuration Initialization and Update Flow\n\n```\n1. Controller starts → lockAndDigestConfigObjects() [apf_controller.go ~300]\n   ├─ Read all FlowSchema objects, sort by increasing numerical precedence\n   ├─ Read all PriorityLevelConfiguration objects\n   └─ For each PriorityLevel:\n      ├─ Create Integrator for seat demand\n      ├─ Create Metrics (RatioedGaugePair for requests, RatioedGauge for seats)\n      └─ Invoke QueueSetFactory.BeginConstruction() → QueueSetCompleter.Complete()\n         → Create queueSet with initial queue count (DesiredNumQueues)\n\n2. Informer event (FlowSchema or PriorityLevelConfiguration change)\n   └─ configQueue.Add(0) → trigger reprocessing\n\n3. Worker loop processes config queue\n   └─ lockAndDigestConfigObjects() with new objects\n      ├─ BeginConfigChange() on existing QueueSet if reconfiguring\n      └─ Call Complete() with new DispatchingConfig (updated concurrency limits)\n```\n\n**Key File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go:277-360`\n\n### 3.2 Request Arrival and Classification Flow\n\n```\nREQUEST ARRIVES\n    ↓\napf_filter.Handle() [apf_filter.go:155-198]\n    ├─ Extract RequestDigest (user, requestInfo)\n    ├─ Iterate flowSchemas in order (by precedence)\n    │  └─ Call matchesFlowSchema() [rule.go:30-37]\n    │     └─ For each PolicyRule in FlowSchema.Spec.Rules:\n    │        ├─ matchesASubject() - user/group/service account matching\n    │        └─ matchesResourceRule() or matchesANonResourceRule()\n    │           └─ Check verbs, resources, API groups, namespaces\n    │\n    ├─ On first match: extract PriorityLevelConfiguration name\n    │\n    ├─ Call workEstimator() [request/width.go:107-136]\n    │  ├─ For LIST requests: listWorkEstimator estimates by object count\n    │  ├─ For WATCH requests: if WatchList feature enabled, use listWorkEstimator\n    │  ├─ For CREATE/UPDATE/PATCH/DELETE: mutatingWorkEstimator estimates by watcher count\n    │  └─ Otherwise: return MinimumSeats (1 seat by default)\n    │\n    └─ Call QueueSet.StartRequest() [queueset.go:308-356]\n```\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go:155-203`\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/rule.go:28-149`\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go:107-136`\n\n### 3.3 Queuing and Virtual Time Fairness Flow\n\n```\nQueueSet.StartRequest() [queueset.go:308-356]\n    ├─ STEP 0: If DesiredNumQueues < 1 (no queuing, concurrency-limit-only)\n    │  ├─ Check if request seats can fit in remaining concurrency limit\n    │  ├─ If NO → reject; metrics.AddReject(..., \"concurrency-limit\")\n    │  └─ If YES → dispatchSansQueueLocked() - execute immediately\n    │\n    ├─ STEP 1: Shuffle sharding and enqueuing\n    │  ├─ shuffleShardLocked(hashValue) [queueset.go:583-612]\n    │  │  ├─ Use Dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue) to select candidate queues\n    │  │  ├─ Pick offset = enqueues % handSize (round-robin across hand)\n    │  │  └─ Select queue with minimum total work (TotalWorkSum)\n    │  │\n    │  └─ shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked() [queueset.go:552-579]\n    │     ├─ Create request struct with arrivalR = currentR (current virtual time)\n    │     ├─ Check if request must be rejected:\n    │     │  └─ (totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit) AND (queue.Length >= QueueLengthLimit)\n    │     └─ If OK → enqueueToBoundLocked() [queueset.go:632-651]\n    │        ├─ If queue was empty: set queue.nextDispatchR = currentR\n    │        ├─ Add request to queue.requestsWaiting (FIFO)\n    │        ├─ Update metrics\n    │        └─ Create removal function for the request\n    │\n    ├─ STEP 2: Dispatch as much as possible\n    │  └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() [queueset.go:653-657]\n    │     └─ While (requests waiting) AND (seats < limit):\n    │        └─ dispatchLocked() [queueset.go:695-743]\n    │           ├─ findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked() [queueset.go:776-822]\n    │           │  ├─ Round-robin through queues\n    │           │  └─ Select queue with minimum (nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork)\n    │           │     = minimum virtual finish time\n    │           │\n    │           └─ Execute selected request:\n    │              ├─ Remove from queue.requestsWaiting\n    │              ├─ Add to queue.requestsExecuting\n    │              ├─ Update queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n    │              └─ Signal promise.Set(decisionExecute)\n    │\n    └─ Return request handle to caller\n\nREQUEST EXECUTION AND FINISH\n    ↓\nrequest.Finish(execFn) [queueset.go:381-395]\n    ├─ request.wait() [queueset.go:397-441]\n    │  ├─ Wait on decision promise (blocked until dispatch or timeout)\n    │  ├─ On decisionExecute: return true, execute request\n    │  └─ On decisionCancel (timeout): return false, reject with \"time-out\"\n    │\n    └─ If executed:\n       └─ finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible() [queueset.go ~900]\n          ├─ Remove request from queue.requestsExecuting\n          ├─ Adjust queue.nextDispatchR for actual service time (if different from estimate)\n          └─ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() (cascade dispatch to next queued request)\n```\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:301-356` (StartRequest)\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:583-612` (shuffleShardLocked)\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:695-743` (dispatchLocked)\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:776-822` (findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked)\n\n### 3.4 Virtual Time Advancement\n\nAt each request arrival, the queueSet synchronizes virtual time:\n\n```\nlockAndSyncTime(ctx) [queueset.go:456-459]\n    └─ syncTimeLocked(ctx) [queueset.go:465-479]\n       ├─ timeSinceLast = clock.Now() - lastRealTime\n       ├─ incrR = SeatsTimesDuration(getVirtualTimeRatio(), timeSinceLast)\n       │  where virtualTimeRatio = min(C, sum(executing_seats)) / activeQueues\n       │                         = min(C, sum of request widths currently executing) / count(non-empty queues)\n       │\n       ├─ currentR += incrR\n       │\n       └─ If currentR >= highR (overflow check):\n          └─ advanceEpoch() [queueset.go:492-522]\n             ├─ Subtract rDecrement from currentR and all queue/request R values\n             └─ Emit metrics.AddEpochAdvance() for overflow tracking\n```\n\n**Key Insight:** Virtual time advances proportionally to the number of active seats relative to the number of active queues. If all C seats are occupied and all queues are active, virtual time advances at rate C nanoseconds per real nanosecond. If fewer seats or queues are active, time advances proportionally slower.\n\n**Key File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:461-522`\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### Request Rejection Paths\n\n1. **Concurrency Limit Exceeded** (`canAccommodateSeatsLocked()` [queueset.go:748-769])\n   - Condition: `totSeatsInUse + requestSeats > ConcurrencyLimit`\n   - Exception: If total executing requests == 0, allow a single request even if > limit (allows single fat request)\n   - Metric: `metrics.AddReject(..., \"concurrency-limit\")`\n\n2. **Queue Length and Concurrency Both at Limit** (`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked()` [queueset.go:614-629])\n   - Condition: `(totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit) AND (queue.Length >= QueueLengthLimit)`\n   - Reason: Cannot enqueue and cannot execute due to both limits\n   - Metric: `metrics.AddReject(..., \"queue-full\")`\n\n3. **Request Timeout While Queued** (`request.wait()` [queueset.go:397-441])\n   - Condition: Context.Cancel() or context deadline exceeded before dispatch\n   - Action: Remove from queue, decrement wait/seat counts\n   - Metric: `metrics.AddReject(..., \"time-out\")`, `totRequestsCancelled++`\n\n#### Virtual Time Overflow Protection\n\n- **Problem:** `currentR` is a `SeatSeconds` (float64) that grows indefinitely\n- **Solution:** `advanceEpoch()` [queueset.go:492-522] subtracts `rDecrement` (MaxSeatSeconds / 2) when `currentR >= highR`\n- **Safety:** All queue `nextDispatchR` and request `arrivalR` values are decremented correspondingly\n- **Metric:** `metrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)` logs overflow count\n\n### 4.2 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Virtual Time Ratio Calculation (getVirtualTimeRatioLocked) [queueset.go:526-541]\n\n**Tradeoff:** Using sum of seat demands across all queues vs. per-queue calculation\n\n```go\n// Current implementation\nseatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)\nreturn min(C, seatsRequested) / activeQueues\n```\n\n**Why:** Ensures fair-queuing fairness across queues based on actual work intensity. A queue with requests requiring many seats (e.g., large list operations) advances its virtual time slower if there are competing queues.\n\n**Tradeoff Impact:**\n- **Pro:** Favors queues with light requests over queues with heavy requests\n- **Con:** Adds per-request work estimate dependency; inaccurate estimates degrade fairness\n\n#### Shuffle Sharding Parameters (HandSize) [queueset.go:583-612]\n\n**Tradeoff:** Randomness vs. queue selection quality\n\n```go\nhand := qs.dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])  // HandSize candidate queues\noffset := qs.enqueues % len(hand)                        // Round-robin offset\nbestQueueIdx = hand[selected]                            // Minimum work queue\n```\n\n**Why:** Introduces entropy to distribute flows and reduce head-of-line blocking for correlated flows while maintaining fairness through minimum-work selection.\n\n**Tradeoff Impact:**\n- **Pro:** Prevents hash collisions from starving unrelated flows\n- **Con:** Slightly unpredictable queue assignments; requires careful tuning of HandSize\n\n#### Initial Work Estimate vs. Actual Service Duration [queueset.go:131-146]\n\n**Tradeoff:** Dispatch latency vs. long-term fairness\n\n```go\ncompletedWorkEstimate = {\n    totalWork: computeInitialWork(we) + computeFinalWork(we)\n    finalWork: SeatsTimesDuration(FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency)\n}\n```\n\n**Why:** Dispatch decisions use estimated work, but actual service time is unknown. After execution completes, queue.nextDispatchR is adjusted by the actual work delta.\n\n**Tradeoff Impact:**\n- **Pro:** Allows immediate dispatch decisions without blocking on actual timing\n- **Con:** Under- or over-estimation causes transient fairness deviations that are corrected over time\n\n#### Concurrency Limit Allocation Strategy [conc_alloc.go:119-257]\n\n**Tradeoff:** Fair proportion allocation vs. constraint satisfaction\n\nThe `computeConcurrencyAllocation()` function solves:\n```\nMinimize deviation from fairProp × target[i] for each class\nSubject to: lowerBound[i] ≤ alloc[i] ≤ upperBound[i]\n           Sum(alloc[i]) = totalConcurrency\n```\n\n**Why:** Allocates concurrency fairly among priority levels while respecting operational constraints (e.g., system-critical priority level has minimum concurrency floor).\n\n**Tradeoff Impact:**\n- **Pro:** Respects both fairness and safety bounds\n- **Con:** Complex algorithm; can be unintuitive when bounds are tight\n\n#### Seat Demand Smoothing (seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977) [apf_controller.go:88]\n\n**Tradeoff:** Responsiveness vs. stability of borrowing adjustments\n\n```go\nsmoothed = max(envelope, A*smoothed + (1-A)*envelope)\n           where envelope = avg + stdDev, A = 0.977\n```\n\n**Why:** Reduces thrashing in borrowing decisions; half-life ~5 minutes (initial design guess).\n\n**Tradeoff Impact:**\n- **Pro:** Prevents borrowing oscillations under bursty load\n- **Con:** Slow reaction to sustained demand changes; may under-allocate during ramps\n\n---\n\n## 5. Operational Implications and Observability\n\n### 5.1 Request Lifecycle Metrics\n\nThe subsystem emits comprehensive metrics at each stage:\n\n| Metric | When Emitted | Semantic |\n|--------|-------------|----------|\n| `requests_in_queues` | Enqueue, Dispatch, Reject | Count of requests waiting in queues |\n| `seats_in_queues` | Enqueue, Dispatch, Reject | Total seat-seconds allocated to waiting requests |\n| `requests_executing` | Dispatch, Finish | Count of executing requests |\n| `seat_concurrency_in_use` | Dispatch, Finish | Total seats occupied (real-time) |\n| `seat_demand` | Every sync interval | Time-weighted integral of occupied + queued seats |\n| `waiting_duration` | Dispatch or Reject | Time from arrival to dispatch or rejection |\n| `execution_duration` | Finish | Time from dispatch to completion |\n| `queue_length` | Per-queue snapshot | Requests waiting in each queue |\n| `epoch_advance_total` | Virtual time overflow | Count of R overflow events |\n\n**Key File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics/metrics.go`\n\n### 5.2 Queue State Introspection\n\nThe `Dump()` method [queueset.go:822] snapshots the internal state for debugging:\n\n```go\ntype QueueSetDump struct {\n    Queues     []QueueDump       // Per-queue state\n    Waiting    int               // Total requests waiting\n    Executing  int               // Total requests executing\n    Dispatched int               // Cumulative dispatched count\n    Rejected   int               // Cumulative rejected count\n    Timedout   int               // Cumulative timeout count\n    Cancelled  int               // Cumulative cancel count\n}\n\ntype QueueDump struct {\n    NextDispatchR     string                 // Queue's virtual start time (stringified)\n    Requests          []RequestDump          // Waiting requests with arrival times\n    RequestsExecuting int                    // Count executing from this queue\n    SeatsInUse        int                    // Seats occupied in this queue\n    QueueSum          struct {\n        InitialSeatsSum  int                 // Sum of request initial seats\n        MaxSeatsSum      int                 // Sum of request max seats\n        TotalWorkSum     string               // Total work in seat-seconds\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis is leveraged by the controller's debug endpoints in `apf_controller_debug.go`.\n\n### 5.3 Concurrency Borrowing Behavior\n\nThe `priorityLevelState` maintains `seatDemandStats` [apf_controller.go:255-260] updated periodically (~10 seconds):\n\n```go\nseatDemandStats {\n    avg            // Time-weighted average seats in use\n    stdDev         // Standard deviation\n    highWatermark  // Peak seats observed\n    smoothed       // Exponentially smoothed envelope (avg + stdDev)\n}\n```\n\nPeriodically, the controller invokes `computeConcurrencyAllocation()` to adjust per-level concurrency limits based on smoothed demand, allowing overloaded levels to borrow from idle levels while maintaining global concurrency.\n\n**Operational Insight:** Monitor `seat_demand_ratio` (seat_demand / nominalCL) per priority level:\n- Ratio ~1.0: Level is operating near capacity; may benefit from higher nominalCL or lower queue limits\n- Ratio >> 1.0: Level is heavily borrowing; consider increasing nominalCL or reducing incoming load\n- Ratio << 1.0: Level is underutilized; concurrency may be wasted; consider borrowing rules\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 6.1 Work Estimator Customization\n\nThe `WorkEstimator` interface [request/width.go:89] allows custom estimation logic:\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimatorFunc func(request *http.Request,\n    flowSchemaName, priorityLevelName string) WorkEstimate\n\n// Implementation per verb:\n// - LIST: objectCountFn(resource) → list object count → estimate seats\n// - WATCH: (with WatchList) same as LIST\n// - MUTATING: watchCountFn(requestInfo) → watcher count → estimate seats\n// - Others: minimumSeats (default 1)\n```\n\n**Extension Risk:** Inaccurate estimation → unfair dispatch order; requests with overestimated seats starve those with underestimated seats.\n\n**Mitigation:** Separate `InitialSeats` (dispatch time estimate) and `FinalSeats` (true final resource demand); post-execution adjustment via actual service time.\n\n**Key Files:**\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go`\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/list_work_estimator.go`\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/mutating_work_estimator.go`\n\n### 6.2 Flow Distinguisher Method\n\nFlowSchema `DistinguisherMethod` [api/flowcontrol/v1] allows custom flow partitioning:\n\n```\nDistinguisherMethod {\n  type: \"ByUser\" | \"ByNamespace\" | \"ByUserAndNamespace\" | ...\n}\n```\n\nThis determines the `hashValue` used in shuffle sharding; different distinguishers route correlated flows to different queues.\n\n**Extension Risk:** Poorly chosen distinguisher → hash collisions → queue imbalance.\n\n### 6.3 Priority Level Configuration\n\n`PriorityLevelConfiguration` allows tuning:\n\n```go\ntype PriorityLevelConfigurationSpec struct {\n    Type: \"Exempt\" | \"Limited\"\n    Limited: {\n        NominalConcurrencyLimit: 100        // Target seats\n        BorrowingLimit: 50                   // Max borrow from pool\n        LendablePercent: 20                  // % available for borrowing\n    }\n    Queuing: {\n        DesiredNumQueues: 16                 // Number of queues\n        QueueLengthLimit: 50                 // Per-queue waiting limit\n        HandSize: 8                          // Shuffle sharding hand size\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Tuning Impacts:**\n- High `DesiredNumQueues` → better isolation, higher memory cost\n- High `HandSize` → lower collision probability, slightly slower queue selection\n- High `QueueLengthLimit` → more buffering, higher rejection latency variability\n\n### 6.4 Promise Factory (Testing Hook)\n\nThe `promiseFactory` [queueset.go:44, 361-362] allows injection of custom promise implementations for testing:\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n\n// Ordinaryimplementation uses promise.NewWriteOnce, a simple write-once pattern\n// Tests can inject mock implementations to simulate timeouts, race conditions, etc.\n```\n\n**Key File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/`\n\n---\n\n## 7. Algorithmic Fairness Guarantees and Tradeoffs\n\n### 8.1 Fair Queuing Bound\n\nTraditional fair queuing provides: _divergence from ideal ≤ 1 packet_\n\nAdapted for concurrent requests: _divergence from ideal ≤ C requests_\n\n**Meaning:** Under virtual time fairness, the actual service received by queue i can diverge from its fair share by at most C request executions. This bound degrades gracefully under:\n- High concurrency limits (C is large)\n- Long-running requests (single request dominates dispatch time)\n\n### 8.2 Virtual Time Computation\n\nKey formula [queueset.go:526-541]:\n\n```\nvirtualTimeRate = min(C, sum(active_request_seats)) / activeQueues\ncurrentR += virtualTimeRate × realTimeDelta\n```\n\n**Fairness Property:**\n- If all C seats are full and N queues are active, each queue advances at rate C/N nanoseconds/real-nanosecond\n- Virtual start times ensure that queues with less work get priority for dispatch\n- Round-robin selection among tied minimum virtual finish times provides FIFO fairness within a queue\n\n### 8.3 Entropy Introduction via Shuffle Sharding\n\nDespite deterministic queue selection (minimum work), shuffle sharding's randomness [queueset.go:583-612] ensures:\n\n1. **Hash collision reduction:** Different flows map to different queues probabilistically\n2. **Correlated request isolation:** Related requests don't all go to the same queue\n3. **Bounded latency variance:** Worst-case queue length is O(total_queue_length / num_queues)\n\n**Tradeoff:** Determinism (reproducibility) vs. robustness (no worst-case collision patterns).\n\n---\n\n## 9. Summary of Critical Implementation Details\n\n### 9.1 Lock Ordering and Concurrency Safety\n\nAll mutable QueueSet state is guarded by `qs.lock` (sync.Mutex) [queueset.go:97]:\n\n```\nMethods acquiring lock:\n  - lockAndSyncTime() - Always called before modifying queue state\n  - IsIdle()\n  - Dump()\n\nMethods assuming lock is held:\n  - *Locked suffix: syncTimeLocked, dispatchLocked, etc.\n\nLock lifecycle:\n  - Held during entire StartRequest() call\n  - Released during request.wait() and execFn() execution\n  - Re-acquired in request.Finish() to update state\n```\n\n**Safety:** No concurrent dispatch or virtual time updates to the same queueset.\n\n### 9.2 Virtual Time Invariants\n\n1. **Monotonicity:** `currentR` never decreases (except advanceEpoch subtracts uniformly)\n2. **Queue ordering:** If queue A has fewer waiting requests than queue B, and both arrive at same time, queue A's nextDispatchR ≤ queue B's nextDispatchR\n3. **Progress:** currentR increases as long as there are executing requests or waiting requests with active queues\n\n### 9.3 Request Lifecycle State Machine\n\n```\nRequest Lifecycle:\n  CREATED → ENQUEUED → DECIDED → EXECUTED/REJECTED\n\nStates:\n  - decision promise: nil → decisionExecute | decisionCancel\n  - queue position: in waitingList → in executingSet | removed\n  - startTime: unset until dispatch\n  - waitStarted flag: prevents double-wait\n\nEdge cases:\n  - Request never waited on (filtered/rejected before startRequest returns)\n  - Request cancelled between enqueue and dispatch (decision = decisionCancel)\n  - Request times out in queue (wait() receives decisionCancel on timeout)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 10. Key Performance Considerations\n\n### 10.1 Dispatch Selection Cost\n\n`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()` [queueset.go:776-822] is O(num_queues):\n\n```go\nfor range qs.queues {                    // O(num_queues)\n    queue := qs.queues[qs.robinIndex]\n    currentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\n    if currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n        minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n        minQueue = queue\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Impact:** With many queues, dispatch becomes a bottleneck. Typical deployments use O(10-100) queues per priority level.\n\n### 10.2 Shuffle Sharding Cost\n\nDealer.DealIntoHand() [external] is O(HandSize) per request, where HandSize is typically 8.\n\n**Impact:** Negligible compared to dispatch selection.\n\n### 10.3 Memory Footprint\n\nPer QueueSet:\n- **Queues:** DesiredNumQueues × (waitingList + executingSet) → O(DesiredNumQueues × QueueLengthLimit)\n- **Metrics:** RatioedGaugePair + RatioedGauge + Integrator → O(1) per priority level\n- **Virtual time tracking:** O(num_executing_requests) for tracking actualwork\n\n**Typical:** 1-10 MB per QueueSet under load.\n\n---\n\n## 11. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem provides **weighted fair queuing** for Kubernetes API server requests through:\n\n1. **Virtual time fairness:** Queue progress proportional to concurrency weight, isolated from real-time variations\n2. **Adaptive queuing:** Shuffle sharding reduces hash collisions; per-queue management enables fine-grained flow control\n3. **Work heterogeneity:** Seat-based estimates accommodate diverse request costs (list vs. simple get)\n4. **Borrowing:** Dynamic concurrency allocation respects priority levels while allowing oversubscribed workloads\n5. **Observability:** Comprehensive metrics and dump endpoints enable operational debugging\n\nThe implementation balances **algorithmic correctness** (fair queuing bounds, virtual time monotonicity) with **operational pragmatism** (grace under overload, efficient dispatch, customization hooks).\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3147,"cache_read_input_tokens":90515,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3147},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ef71afa5-d1cf-4452-bf6b-bd7777fb1002","uuid":"c7eb8101-357e-4a14-90a8-deeb9563d9a0"}
